\begin{letter}{B}

\fmtLemma{ba-}%
\fmtOne{1}
\fmtPOS{pf}
\fmtSense{object agreement prefix of the second person plural on verbs}

\fmtLemma{ba-}%
\fmtOne{2}
\fmtPOS{pf}
\fmtSense{subject and object agreement prefix of class 2 on verbs}

\fmtLemma{baa\-ba}
\fmtPOS{interj}
\fmtSense{oh dear, my goodness, oh my}
\fmtExampleRL{Oh baa\-ba afii\-re!}
\fmtExampleEN{Oh dear, he has died!}
\fmtSense{elder sibling}
\fmtExampleRL{Obaa\-ba wa\-nge ansi\-nga\-ku emya\-ka isa\-tu.}
\fmtExampleEN{My elder sibling is three years older than me.}

\fmtLemma{baa\-bwe}
\fmtCrossreference{\textnormal{see} abwe}

\fmtLemma{baa\-ga}
\fmtCitation{(oku)\-baa\-ga}
\fmtPOS{v}%
\fmtTrans{tr}
\fmtPFV{baa\-gi\-re}
\fmtSubentry(a)
\fmtSense{to skin (an animal), to flay}
\fmtExampleRL{Mba\-le\-ke\-re\-yo eka nga ba\-ku\-baa\-ga onte.}
\fmtExampleEN{I have left them at home skinning a cow.}
\fmtSubentry(b)
\fmtSense{to slaughter, to butcher}
\fmtExampleRL{Ombu\-li oyo ali\-na ei\-wa\-ko ti\-mu\-ku\-so\-bo\-la ku\-mu\-baa\-ga.}
\fmtExampleEN{That goat is pregnant, you cannot have it slaughtered.}
\fmtSubentry(c)
\fmtSense{to cut up, to dismember, to dissect}
\fmtSubentry(d)
\fmtSense{to operate on}

\fmtLemma{baa\-laa\-la}
\fmtCitation{(oku)\-baa\-laa\-la}
\fmtPOS{v}%
\fmtTrans{intr}
\fmtPFV{baa\-laa\-lii\-re}
\fmtSense{(of chilli pepper) to be hot, to be spicy}
\fmtExampleRL{Oka\-mu\-la\-li omu\-doo\-li abaa\-laa\-la mu\-no.}
\fmtExampleEN{The chilli pepper is very hot.}

\fmtLemma{baa\-li\-kya\-tu\-la}
\fmtCitation{(e)baa\-li\-kya\-tu\-la}
\fmtPOS{n}%
\fmtNC{9/10}
\fmtSense{pot used for drinking millet brew}
\fmtExampleRL{Omu\-sai\-za aya\-ti\-rye ebaa\-li\-kya\-tu\-la ya\-nge.}
\fmtExampleEN{The man has broken my pot for drinking millet brew.}

\fmtLemma{baa\-mu}
\fmtCrossreference{\textnormal{see} amu}

\fmtLemma{baa\-mwe\-(i)}
\fmtCrossreference{\textnormal{see} amwe\textnormal{{\fmtOne{1}}}}

\fmtLemma{baa\-nywe}
\fmtCrossreference{\textnormal{see} nywe}

\fmtLemma{ba\-bii\-ra}
\fmtCitation{(oku)\-ba\-bii\-ra}
\fmtPOS{v}%
\fmtTrans{intr}
\fmtPFV{ba\-bii\-ri\-re}
\fmtSubentry(a)
\fmtSense{to feel a burning sensation (as a result of the contact with something hot or irritating)}
\fmtExampleRL{Amai\-zi aga\-yo we ga\-nsu\-ku\-ki\-re\-ku, wa\-ku\-mba\-bii\-ra.}
\fmtExampleEN{I feel a burning sensation where I got burnt with hot water.}
\fmtSubentry(b)
\fmtSense{to have a peppery taste}
\fmtExampleRL{Ka\-la\-li aba\-bii\-ra mu\-no.}
\fmtExampleEN{The pepper has a peppery taste.}

\fmtLemma{ba\-bi\-ru\-mi\-ra\-ki}
\fmtCitation{(o)ba\-bi\-ru\-mi\-ra\-ki}
\fmtPOS{n}%
\fmtNC{1a}
\fmtSense{destructive wind (lit.\,why did we grow them),  hurricane}
\fmtExampleRL{Oba\-bi\-ru\-mi\-ra\-ki asii\-si\-re endu\-mi\-ro za mwa\-ni zai\-swe.}
\fmtExampleEN{The destructive wind has destroyed our coffee plantations.}

\fmtLemma{ba\-bu\-ka}
\fmtCitation{(oku)\-ba\-bu\-ka}
\fmtPOS{v}%
\fmtTrans{intr}
\fmtPFV{ba\-bu\-ki\-re}
\fmtSense{to be scorched, to become burnt (on the surface), to singe, to become singed}
\fmtExampleRL{Amai\-do gai\-swe ga\-ba\-bu\-ki\-re.}
\fmtExampleEN{Our groundnuts are scorched.}

\fmtLemma{ba\-bu\-la}
\fmtCitation{(oku)\-ba\-bu\-la}
\fmtPOS{v}%
\fmtTrans{tr}
\fmtPFV{ba\-bwi\-re}
\fmtSubentry(a)
\fmtSense{to singe}
\fmtExampleRL{Ba\-bu\-la onko\-ko oyo nga tu\-kya\-li ku\-mu\-baa\-ga.}
\fmtExampleEN{Singe the chicken before we cook it.}
\fmtSubentry(b)
\fmtFixedexpression{babula (e)njoka}
\fmtSense{not to gain from something (lit.\,to burn a snake)}
\fmtExampleRL{Olwa\-lee\-ro mba\-bwi\-re njo\-ka.}
\fmtExampleEN{Today I have not gained anything.}

\fmtLemma{ba\-bu\-lya}
\fmtCitation{(oku)\-ba\-bu\-lya}
\fmtPOS{v}%
\fmtTrans{tr}
\fmtPFV{ba\-bwi\-rye}
\fmtSense{to singe, to scorch, to remove the hair or bristle of pigs (\eg by covering it in grass and putting it on fire)}
\fmtExampleRL{Ba\-bu\-lya\-ku onko\-ko azwe\-ku obwo\-ya.}
\fmtExampleEN{Singe the chicken so that the feathers will come off.}

\fmtLemma{ba\-buu\-kii\-ra}
\fmtCitation{(oku)\-ba\-buu\-kii\-ra}
\fmtPOS{v}%
\fmtTrans{intr}
\fmtPFV{ba\-buu\-kii\-re}
\fmtSense{to feel a burning sensation}
\fmtExampleRL{Ni nei\-sii\-sii\-rya ama\-gi\-ta ga\-ni ga\-mba\-buu\-kii\-ra.}
\fmtExampleEN{When I smear myself with this vaseline, I feel a burning sensation.}

\fmtLemma{ba\-da}
\fmtCitation{(oku)\-ba\-da}
\fmtPOS{v}%
\fmtTrans{tr}
\fmtPFV{ba\-di\-re}
\fmtSense{to weave a wall frame using reeds}
\fmtExampleRL{Naa\-ni ya\-ba\-di\-re enyu\-mba eni?}

\fmtLemma{ba\-di}
\fmtCrossreference{\textnormal{see} di}

\fmtLemma{ba\-ga\-na}
\fmtCitation{(oku)\-ba\-ga\-na}
\fmtPOS{v}%
\fmtTrans{tr}
\fmtPFV{ba\-gai\-ne}
\fmtSubentry(a)
\fmtSense{to share, to divide}
\fmtExampleRL{Mwi\-ze tu\-ba\-ga\-ne eki\-ba\-nja kyai\-swe.}

\fmtSubentry(b)
\fmtSense{(of gospel) to share the word of God}

\fmtLemma{ba\-ga\-nya}
\fmtCitation{(oku)\-ba\-ga\-nya}
\fmtPOS{v}
\fmtTrans{tr}
\fmtPFV{ba\-gai\-nye}
\fmtSubentry(a)
\fmtSense{to share, to divide}
\fmtExampleRL{Ba\-ga\-nya ame\-nju ga\-ni omu bai\-raa\-mu.}
\fmtExampleEN{Divide these bananas among your friends.}
\fmtSubentry(b)
\fmtFixedexpression{baganya (e)birowoozo}
\fmtSense{to have an exchange of ideas, to have a discussion, to debate}
\fmtExampleRL{Oku\-ku\-ba\-ga\-nya ebi\-ri\-woo\-zo kwa\-twi\-re olu\-na\-ku lu\-la\-mbii\-ra.}
\fmtExampleEN{The debate was prolonged for the whole day.}

\fmtLemma{Ba\-go\-nza}
\fmtCitation{(o)Ba\-go\-nza}
\fmtPOS{n}
\fmtNC{1a}
\fmtSense{name given to a child whose mother is not liked by the husband's family}
\fmtExampleRL{Ba\-go\-nza iba\-ra li\-wee\-bwa omwa\-na nga abee\-ka ya mu\-sai\-za te\-ba\-ku\-mu\-ta\-ka.}
\fmtExampleEN{Bagonza is a name given to a child whose mother is not liked by the husband's family.}

\fmtLemma{ba\-la\-ngu\-la}

\fmtSubentry(b)
\fmtSense{to hit hard}

\fmtExampleEN{He was hit hard with a stick and died from it instantly.}

\fmtSense{to brew (concentrated alcoholic beverages)}
\fmtExampleRL{Omu\-yii\-sya ya\-ba\-la\-ngwi\-re ama\-lwa.}
\fmtExampleEN{The brewer brewed very concentrated finger millet beer.}

\fmtLemma{bba}
\fmtCitation{(oku)\-bba}
\fmtPOS{v}%
\fmtTrans{intr}
\fmtPFV{bbai\-re}
\fmtSubentry(a)
\fmtSense{to be, to exist}
\fmtExampleRL{Ka\-nca abba bu\-li amwe.}
\fmtExampleEN{God exists everywhere.}
\fmtSubentry(b)

\fmtSense{period of childhood after breastfeeding}
\fmtExampleRL{Obu\-ncuu\-ki\-re bwa Edwa\-rd bwa\-li\-wo kwa nza\-la.}
\fmtExampleEN{In the period when Edward stopped breastfeeding, there was famine.}

\fmtLemma{bu\-ndaa\-la}
\fmtCitation{(oku)\-bu\-ndaa\-la}
\fmtPOS{v}%
\fmtTrans{intr}
\fmtPFV{bu\-ndai\-re}
\fmtSubentry(a)
\fmtSense{to sag, to slump, to sank, to go down}
\fmtExampleRL{Olu\-ka\-nga\-ga lu\-bu\-ndai\-re lu\-ku\-ta\-ka ku\-gwa\-mu.}
\fmtExampleEN{The sagging roof is threatening to collapse.}
\fmtSubentry(b)
\fmtSense{(of pet animals) to lie down showing loyalty, to prostrate oneself}
\fmtExampleRL{Ombwe\-ne abu\-ndai\-re egi\-ri mu\-ka\-ma waa\-mwe.}
\fmtExampleEN{The dog is prostrating itself before its master.}

\fmtLemma{bu\-nda\-ma}
\fmtCitation{(oku)\-bu\-nda\-ma}
\fmtPOS{v}%
\fmtTrans{intr}
\fmtPFV{bu\-nda\-mi\-re}
\fmtSubentry(a)
\fmtSense{(of animals) to take cover}
\fmtExampleRL{Onja\-ngwa abu\-nda\-ma nga aku\-tye\-ka ome\-se.}
\fmtExampleEN{The cat takes cover while waiting for a rat.}
\fmtSubentry(b)
\fmtSense{to sink, to collapse}
\fmtExampleRL{Enyu\-mba ya Ka\-ra\-ngwa ebu\-ndai\-me.}
\fmtExampleEN{Karangwa’s house has collapsed.}
\fmtSubentry(c)
\fmtSense{(of a person) to prostrate, to bow low, to throw oneself at someone's feet}
\fmtExampleRL{Ka\-ba\-ka wa Bu\-ga\-nda ba\-mu\-bu\-ndaa\-mi\-ra.}
\fmtExampleEN{They prostrate themselves before the king of Buganda.}

\fmtLemma{bya\-nke\-nga}
\fmtCitation{(e)bya\-nke\-nga}
\fmtPOS{n}%
\fmtNC{8}
\fmtSubentry(a)
\fmtSense{forecast, prediction}
\fmtSubentry(b)
\fmtFixedexpression{bya\-nke\-nga ya bwi\-re}
\fmtSense{weather forecast}
\fmtExampleRL{Nku\-so\-ma ku bya\-nke\-nga ya bwi\-re.}
\fmtExampleEN{I am reading the weather forecast.}

\fmtLemma{bya\-ntu\-nga}
\fmtCitation{(e)bya\-ntu\-nga}
\fmtPOS{n}%
\fmtNC{8}
\fmtSense{economic development}
\fmtExampleRL{Ebya\-ntu\-nga byai\-swe bya\-sii\-si\-kai\-re.}
\fmtExampleEN{Our economic development is delayed.}

\fmtLemma{bya\-nye\-ge\-sya}
\fmtCitation{(e)bya\-nye\-ge\-sya}
\fmtPOS{n}%
\fmtNC{8}
\fmtSense{education, schooling}
\fmtExampleRL{Ebya\-nye\-ge\-sya omu di\-si\-tu\-li\-ki\-ti yai\-swe ti\-bi\-sai.}
\fmtExampleEN{The standard of education in our district is poor.}

\fmtPOS{n}%
\fmtNC{8}
\fmtSense{history, the past}
\fmtExampleRL{Ebya\-swa\-yo bya Bu\-ruu\-li ti\-bi\-wa\-ndii\-ke ku\-sai.}
\fmtExampleEN{The history of Buruuli is not well documented.}

\fmtExampleRL{Ba\-mu\-na\-gii\-re ebya\-wo\-ngo omu ire\-mbo.}

\fmtPOS{pro}
\fmtSense{they (noun class 8 independent pronoun)}

\fmtLemma{byo\-nzi}
\fmtCitation{(e)byo\-nzi}
\fmtPOS{n}%
\fmtNC{8}
\fmtSense{eye discharge (due to bacterial conjunctivitis)}
\fmtExampleRL{Amai\-so ga\-nge ga\-ku\-ndu\-ma gai\-zi\-re n’e\-byo\-nzi.}
\fmtExampleEN{My eyes are infected and are oozing out discharge.}

\fmtLemma{byo\-ya}
\fmtCitation{(e)byo\-ya}
\fmtPOS{n}%
\fmtNC{8}
\fmtSubentry(a)
\fmtSense{fur, wool}
\fmtExampleRL{Ontaa\-ma abba ne byo\-ya bi\-ngi.}
\fmtExampleEN{The sheep has thick wool.}
\fmtSubentry(b)
\fmtFixedexpression{byo\-ya bya mu nku\-wa}
\fmtSense{armpit hair}
\fmtExampleRL{Omu\-gwai\-ra\-lu ta\-ge\-mba byo\-ya bya mu nku\-wa.}
\fmtExampleEN{The madman does not shave his armpit hair.}
\fmtSubentry(c)
\fmtFixedexpression{byo\-ya bya mu\-nda}
\fmtSense{stomach ulcer}
\fmtExampleRL{Ebi\-ro bi\-ni aba\-ntu bai\-ngi ba\-lwa\-la ebyo\-ya bya mu\-nda.}
\fmtExampleEN{These days, many people suffer from stomach ulcer.}
